text:
These meatballs were a hit!  I used frozen meatballs.
Most jellied cranberry sauce come in 16 oz cans so if you decide to use the whole can you'll need to double all the other ingredients.  Typical chili sauce comes in 12oz. bottle so you'll need two bottles if you use the full can of cranberry.  Hope this helps your  shopping.

text:
I have made these numerous times and am ashamed to admit I'm just now reviewing them.  Wonderful addition to the regular grape jelly recipes out there with great meatballs....      Based on experience and personal preference with these cocktail meatballs I offer the following suggestions:  1.)  Add one packet of lipton onion soup mix to the meatball mixture if you do not have time to mince or grate the onion.  2.)  Bake meatballs over a drip pan to reduce the fat before adding to the sauce.  3.) If using frozen meatballs ENSURE you DO NOT use Italian meatballs as this upsets the balance of the meatballs and sauce (yuck)!  3.)  Make the sauce the day before to let the flavors marry - I can't stress what a difference this makes!  This recipe gets better the next day.  4.)  The Heinz sauce in the round bottle seems to be the best chili sauce for this mixture.  Reviewers:  I seriously dislike people that rate a recipe based on the changes they have made to the original.  I want to state that I rated this recipe on the recipe Lara submitted.  The changes I suggested were based on my family's personal preference.  Thanks Lara for a fabulous appetizer recipe - I always give you the credit!

text:
This is a very tasty recipe for meatballs, with the cranberry sauce representing a change from the run of the mill grape jelly recipe.  I used seasoned bread crumbs, which added some nice flavor to the meatballs, and then baked them on a broiler tray, which allowed the fat to run off while they were baking.  One recipe is enough to fill one of the small 1 to 2 quart crockpots.  I made the meatballs 2 days ahead, and refrigerated them.  The day of my party, I made the sauce, put the meatballs in the crockpot, added the sauce, and put the whole crock back in the fridge.  About 2 hours before the party, I put the crock back in the warmer, and plugged it in.  Voila!  Easy and tasty.  I was so impressed with the recipe, that I made an extra batch of the meatballs, and froze them.  I will use them for another party in the next couple of weeks.  I'll bet you could use ground turkey for a little less fat.  Thanks for sharing a wonderful recipe!

text:
These were great! So great, I barely got to eat 2 of them myself - the guys just inhaled them! One thing that would make the recipe easier though, is some explanation of what is meant by "Chili Sauce". There are so many types of Chili Sauce out there - after searching, I found that Heinz makes something called "Chili Sauce". If you're like me and have never heard of this type of chili sauce, it's basically a vinegar-y, very mildly spiced-up version of ketchup - (sort of like cocktail sauce for shrimp?), w/a ketchup consistency. You can find it next to the ketchup in any big chain grocery. You can't go wrong with this recipe! I'm making it again for New Year's eve!

text:
I'm 67 and this recipe has been around forever... they're always a hit, where ever I take them. Definitely bake the meatballs before adding them to the sauce. I bake mine 25 to 30 minutes. The correct chili sauce is a tomato based chili sauce, such as Heinz or Cross & Blackwell. Sometimes I use grape jelly in place of the cranberry sauce (same amount), also makes a very good sauce. If you are making this for a group, trust me you'll want to double, or even triple the recipe. People don't stop at 4 or 5, they just keep eating them until they're gone... especially the guys... LOL  These are addictive!!!!!

text:
Chili sauce is usually found next to ketchup.  Heinz is the only brand I've seen or used.  It's in a round glass bottle.  It's basically ketchup with a little extra spice, but definitely not anything like tabasco or hot sauce.  If you had to substitute, you could use ketchup with extra onion and garlic added.  Hope this helps!

text:
I've been making a variation of this recipe for 20 years.  It is not overly sweet and is a true sweet & sour.  I hate sauerkraut but love this and nobody can guess that it is in it. It makes a thick sauce. SAUCE: 12 oz. jar Heinz Cili Sauce, i jar of water, 1 cup brown sugar, 16 oz. can WHOLE cranberry sauce, 1 cup drained sauerkraut.  MEATBALLS: 2 lbs. extra lean ground beef, 1 pkg. onion soup mix, 2 eggs, 1 cup bread crumbs.  Form into small meatballs (about 88)  DO NOT BROWN!!  Place in a 9X13 pan, mix sauce ingredients & pour over meatballs.  Bake at 325 degrees for 2 hours.  Check occassionally and stir if necessary.

Very good! 100 times better after the sauce sits over night! I used the Heinz chili sauce (oh & this recipe is on the bottle label...) I tripled the recipe and used frozen meatballs from costco (didnt have the energy or prepare 4-6lbs of meatballs..) The first night they were good, my husband ate em right up but I was not at all impressed. This statement sums it up perfectly: "Word of warning - do NOT use the Italian meatballs! The flavors fight each other and the sauce is the loser" Needless to say I used italian meatballs BEFORE reading the review....the flavors just didnt blend & the sauce was WAY TOO SWEET!!! HOWEVER, after sitting overnight and reheating the next day 100 TIMES BETTER! The flavors of the sauce 'blended' together much better & produced a great flavor that no longer was sooo sweet. Will make again!

Since it seems to baffling some: Chili Sauce is a LOT like cocktail sauce (kick from chili rather than horseradish though, best I can tell). I've only seen it made by Heinz, and it will likely be right beside the cocktail sauce in the grocery store. It is NOT sriracha, or anything you'd put on a hotdog, etc. Hope that helps somebody out!  Made these for an office party. They smelled fantastic while cooking, but I never got to eat one myself - they were scarfed down, to rave reviews, before I got the chance! Will definitely make again.

text:
This is pretty close to my standard recipe, too.  I use whatever I have on hand as the "filler", whether it be bread crumbs, oatmeal, cracker crumbs, leftover cooked rice, etc.  One thing I always had trouble with was that they tended to fall apart once they were in the crockpot with the sauce.  On the advice of a friend, I tried rolling the raw meatballs in flour before browning them in oil.  This method really helps!  I make a huge batch of them, making sure they're cooked through, then line them up on jelly-roll pans and stick them in the freezer.  Once frozen, they can go into zip-lock bags and be handy for whenever I need a quick dish.

These meatballs were gone in a flash! I served them at a dinner party and everyone loved them. I made 5.25 pounds of frozen meat balls (NOT Italian) and 4x the sauce. I cooked them in the crock-pot for four hours on high...it would probably be better to cook for at least six hours on low. The Heinz chili sauce is a 12oz bottle which is 1 cup. For those who might wonder, the Wal-Mart brand of chili sauce is just as good as the Heinz; I bought both and couldn't tell a difference (WM was actually thicker). I made the sauce the day before for ease and so the flavors would meld. You can't go wrong with this recipe, it's a winner!

text:
This is the 1st time I ever attempted meatballs and I really loved these. The sauce was really good. Tripled the recipe and took them to a baby shower. I had very little left over and had some requests for the recipe. 
The funny thing is, the entire time I was adding the sauce ingredients, I kept wrinkling my nose and thinking "this can't be good". I mean, cranberry sauce, chili sauce & lemon juice. Wow. But it was very good. 
I actually made these the day before I needed them. I baked the meatballs on a broiler pan so the grease would drip down and not pool around the meatballs. I then just placed them in a container, poured the sauce over them, put a lid on them and threw them in the fridge. The next morning at 8am, I dumped it all in the slow cooker to heat before the 1:00 baby shower. Perfect. 
The only change I made was adding a bit more minced onions and the bread crumbs were Italian flavored. That little bit of flavor didn't overwhelm the sauce at all.

Yum.  I made these in a crockpot and they came out great.  I bought frozen swedish meatballs from BJ's Wholesale Club.  I would normally make my own meatballs, but was short on time.  These were awesome.  I turned the crockpot on high, added 2 cans of jellied cranberry sauce, a bottle and 1/2 of chile sauce and the remaining ingredients.  When I first saw what the sauce looked like I thought "yuck" this will not be good, but I was so wrong.  I let the sauce get a little warm and then added the meatballs and just left it.  I left it on high for about 4 hours and then stirred and turned it down to low.  I left the crockpot on low all day and throughout the party and they were fine.  They were a big hit and will definitely make again. It's so easy if you buy the meatballs already made!  Great appetizer to bring to a party.

These are tasty and everyone loves at parties. Once I made them for a wedding reception, and two weeks later one of the wedding guests and I saw each other at the store and she was STILL talking about how great the meatballs were-- nothing about the flowers, or the dress, or the music, or the bride and groom! A million thanks-yous for this great recipe.  The cranberry sauce adds a great taste.  Sometimes (depending on the crowd)when I make a large batch, I use half the cranberry sauce and replace the other half with the more traditional grape jelly.  This way works well too.

text:
This has been an extended-family favorite for several years. To cut down on time, I use frozen turkey meatballs (w/o Italian seasoning). Since the recipe only calls for 8 oz cranberry sauce, I use the whole can of whole-berry cranberry sauce, the entire jar of Heinz Chili Sauce, 2 Tb brown sugar, and 1 Tbsp lemon juice; mix the sauce together and pour over the meatballs, and heat in the slow cooker, stirring occasionally. Serve with decorative toothpicks (or plain ones, depending on who's eating them!) with small plates and plenty of napkins. My SIL liked this so much, I gave her the recipe, and now she always serves it when we arrive. Two thumbs up!

My daughter has made them by baking the meatballs first & THEN spooning the sauce over & also, spooning the sauce over & THEN baking them. Both ways are great! I like the sauce spooned over before baking the best!
She brought them tail-gating & they went over better than anything!
Great as a main dish or SNACK! Glad I came across this!

text:
I usually use Costco Italian style meatballs with chili sauce and grape jelly which have always been a crowd-pleaser. I decided to try something different for my step-daughters baby shower with 35 guests.  I decided on this recipe because it was so highly rated and had to triple the recipe.  For the sake of time, I used Lipton onion soup mix as suggested by other reviewers but did not alter the remainder of the recipe in any way.  They probably would have been better with minced onions because the seasonings in the soup mix altered the flavor.  I mistakenly made them twice the size they should have been and ended up with only 55 meatballs, not enough for the party. I asked my husband to do a taste test and he preferred the meatballs I usually make, as did I.  I ended up taking the Costco grape jelly chili sauce meatballs to the party and they were a hit.  They were the food that had no leftovers.  I will stick with my old stand-by.  By the way, a lot of reviewers have advised against using frozen Italian meatballs with this sauce. I think Costco's meatballs would work just fine as the Romano cheese and spices are not over-powering.

text:
I made these once with store bought meatballs and once with the recipe.  The store bought meatball one turned out great.  When I made them from scratch, I used Panko breadcrumbs.  I cooked and cooked them and they just never seemed to really firm up.  Some of them were breaking apart as people tried to scoop them up from the crockpot.  They tasted good but were brittle.

The sauce is really good.  It's pretty sweet, though.    I made the sauce and meatballs separately the night before, mixed them together, and let them sit overnight.  Threw them in the crockpot on low about an hour before the party and it was perfect!  If it weren't for all the extra fat and garbage ingredients they put in storebought meatballs, I would say that's totally the way to go as I didn't feel the flavor was any better in the from scratch ones once the sauce was put on.

text:
Overall, I gave the results a resounding "Eh." Not bad, but not what I was expecting from the other reviews.

The meatball mix sounded bland, so I added a sprinkling of salt, pepper, garlic powder, dried parsley, and red pepper flakes. It tasted OK. I didn't think the onion was overwhelming, as some said, but the meatballs were a little mushy.

I ended up using more chili sauce than the recipe called for because after putting all the meatballs in the crockpot there did not seem to be enough sauce. I bought a small generic bottle from WalMart, and it wasn't too spicy. The finished sauce wasn't bad, it just tasted like sweet & sour sauce from Chinese takeout. I'm not sure I liked it with beef---I might have tried it with ground pork or turkey instead.

I give the recipe as-is only two stars.

text:
Reading the other reviews, I noticed that the happiest outcomes involved store-bought meatballs.  Since I was making my own, I decided to spice up that part of the recipe, adding salt, pepper, garlic powder, snipped fresh parsley, and a tsp. of horseradish.  I still wasn't wowed by the flavor.  I used 93% lean meat and baked the meatballs in the oven for 25 minutes before finishing them off in the crockpot with the sauce for 2 hours.  I didn't have quite enough cranberry sauce on hand so I substituted an equal amount of strawberry-rhubarb jam and left out the brown sugar.  It was sweeter than I prefer, but the party goers to whom I served them seemed content.  I got about 3 dozen small meatballs out of a pound of hamburger.

text:
I made these with ground turkey breast -- the super lean type.  To make the meatballs moist, I soaked fresh bread crumbs in 2 Tbsp half-n-half before mixing with the onion, egg and turkey.  I added 1Tbsp horseradish, a grated carrot and 1tsp salt for extra flavor.  Because the turkey was so lean, instead of baking the meatballs and draining the fat, I simply dropped them raw into the hot sauce in the crock pot and let them cook in the sauce for about 4 hrs on low.    I didn't think the added sugar was needed in the sauce, but they were delicious!

Just a very quick note to "Army Wife."  Tabasco Sauce is in no way, shape or form considered Chili Sauce.  It's a Pepper Sauce.  You will find Chili Sauce right along side Ketchup in most Grocery Stores.  I have not tried this recipe as of yet but from all the reviews it looks like a WINNER!!!  I suggest you try the recipe again but this time with Chili Sauce.  FYI.....The Chili Sauce I use is "Heinz Chili Sauce" but I am sure any brand will do.  Giver 'er a GO!!!!!!!!!

text:
Loved them!

I made homemade cranberry sauce (recipe from here I believe...12 oz cranberries, 1 cup orange juice--or 1/2 water 12 orange juice, 1 cup sugar, cook until berries pop, then mashed with potato masher) instead of the nasty canned stuff.

Also, instead of chili sauce, I used ketchup with a splash of balsamic vinegar, 1 T garlic powder and 1 t minced onions because all the chili sauce options at my grocery store were chock full of high fructose corn syrup.

Because my cranberry sauce comes out so thick, I added a cup of water to the simmering step. I also left out the brown sugar since I used brown sugar in my cranberry sauce.

The meatballs turned out amazing! My mom, the best cook ever, loved them.

Thank you to the recipe author for the inspiration!

Home run!  I made this over Christmas '04, New Years '05 and a recent family gathering. I turn around and they are all gone!  I add a package of Little Smokies for variety. Crockpot on high for the 1st hour and then 2 hrs on low--if you are a crock pot cooker--you'll know how to adjust heat so meatballs don't get too soft.  I use a store brand cranberry sauce as the good stuff seems too sweet!  But this gal has the perfect recipe for a meatball as far as bread crumbs and liquid.  I added some parm cheese and pepper and it was hard not to eat them ALL as they came out of the oven nice and hot and browned...YUMMA!

text:
The meatballs for this recipe are very quick and easy to make, and just dropping them in the sauce to simmer was very convenient.  I would maybe combine the cranberry sauce with a tiny bit of grape jelly, however, as some might find 100% cranberry sauce a bit too tart.  Otherwise, I've noticed that the meatballs just....disappear.  Chop up the onions and such VERY finely, as too chunky pieces will ruin the overall effect.  A little green pepper would be good with these, as well...

Loved these! Although, I can't rate the meatballs, only the sauce. I use the 'Meatball Nirvana' recipe from this site (incredible!!) and the ones on this recipe seem would be a bit bland compared to those. Thats my only reason for not giving this a 5 star rating- the flavor of the actual meatballs outside of the sauce is incredibly important, it can make all the difference between a dry or bland dish underneath the sauce. And if your short on time, it is super easy to grab a package of frozen meatballs, thaw & throw the sauce on top in the crock pot! But the sauce was excellent- this was very well liked and disappeared pretty quickly. Will be saving this for future use, only with a more diverse & flavorful meatball.

I made this recipe, for a holiday party last year.  I used bought turkey meatballs and I made my own cranberry sauce, otherwise followed the instructions. We have about 70 people for an open house, style party, so these meatballs worked out great, because I could keep them in a crockpot on low. Everyone liked them and we were able to freeze the leftovers and have them for a quick meal with a salad, when we didn't have time to cook. One suggestion, I made the sauce the night before, let it cool and then put the meatballs and sauce in big gallon size bags and let them marinate in the fridge overnight. The meatballs stayed very moist.

I made this for a Christmas Eve party and it was an instant hit!  
To make life easier, I made the meatballs a couple weeks ahead and put them in the freezer.  I didn't have fresh onion, so I used the suggestion of another reviewer and just added a package of onion soup mix.  It gave the meatballs a nice spice and made it a little easier to prepare (saved chopping onions/tears!).
I made the sauce the night before - made it exactly to the recipe, no adjustments or substitutions.
At 7am the morning of the event, I put the frozen meatballs in my crockpot, added the sauce and put it on low.  By 2pm (the start of the party) it was bubbling and smelling amazing.  They were an instant hit!  Will be making these again for sure!

text:
These were very good.  I had ground beef in freezer bags in the freezer, so I don't know exactly how much I used, but I'm guessing 2+ pounds.  Then, I used 1 bottle of Heinz Chili Sauce and (1) 14 oz can of cranberry sauce.  I didn't measure the other ingredients (just eye-balled it), but I could definitely still taste the tartness of the cranberries, more in the aftertaste than the actual bite.  I like cranberries, but my husband doesn't (and neither do a lot of our guests).  Since everyone likes sweet party meatballs, I tried adding just a little more brown sugar, and it took the tartness away.  The other thing that I changed was the cooking time.  After cooking in the crockpot on high for 1 hour, the onions in the meatballs still had a slight crunch.  I added another 1-1/2 hours to the crockpot, and they came out moist and delicious.  There weren't many leftovers, but my husband and I made little sandwiches with Hawaiian bread, and it was great!

I agree with a previous person who said to cook them on high in the crockpot for 2 hours prior to serving. I warmed the sauce up in a pot and tasted it and it was pretty bad. text:
My go-to cocktail meatball recipe, because I appreciate homemade meatballs rather than frozen, and I prefer baking them first to cooking raw meatballs in sauce as I sometimes see suggested.  Some very basic additional seasoning - salt, pepper, garlic, soy sauce, parsley perhaps, etc. - would take it to 5 stars; the meatballs as written are sometimes a bit bland, however the delicious sauce makes up for that, and the lack of embellishment to the meat mixture means the children enjoy them, too, and sure keeps preparation simple!  Can be made ahead -always a plus to a hostess.  I've served this recipe on New Year's Eve for several years, and now get requests for Superbowl, Oscar night  and various winter gatherings.  I bet you will, too!

I also added about 1 tblsp Worcestershire. text:
I made this recipe as is for a potluck at work. Most of the time the stuff I bring (recipes from this site) is a huge hit, but since I hadnt made this before, I didnt tell anyone that I broguht the cocktail meatballs. But when I looked around the room, and nobody had them on their plates, because they had eaten them all, I fessed up! Anyway, super easy recipe to make (prepared them the night before and refrigerated until the morning, turned on the crock pot, and finished just in time for lunch!) and even easier to eat! I had never used chili sauce before, but I picked up a few bottles, and have made dozens of the meatballs and froze them so I can whip up this recipe at a moment's notice!! I also used a small cookie scoop to ensure all the meatballs are the same size, and baked the meatballs as directed, but I used a 13x9 pan with an elevated rack to help them cook evenly. PERFECT!!

text:
I have made this a few times so I have some tips.  1) Definitely cook them in the oven first.  This helps them keep the shape so you can actually stir them in the crock pot.  2) Definitely do not use the amount of chili sauce this recipe says to use.  I used the Sriacchi chili sauce (the bottle w/ the rooster) and only did about 1/4 total and I doubled the recipe.  I also like it spicey.  I took others' advice and added ketchup and worchestchire in place of water.  I also added a couple tablespoons of bbq sauce because I had some in the fridge.  I have made this with and without brown sugar and couldn't really tell the difference.  This time I didn't have any brown sugar so I added a squirt of maple syrup although it probably didn't even need it.  This is a great recipe for potlucks and I got great compliments both times I've made it.  Just watch the chili sauce or some peple won't be able to handle it!

text:
I made this over the weekend for a dinner party and as noted in other reviews, they were eaten up! A few things I did with the meatballs: I did double the recipe and used 2 lbs of lean ground beef and added one packet of lipton onion soup mix, a few generaous shots of Worcestershire sauce and used italian seasoned bread crumbs. For the sauce I used the entire can of both the cranberry and chili sauce and added a few dashes of franks hot sauce (the flavor is less intense than Tabasco). But the sauce looked like it wouldn't even be close to enough. So, I threw in half a bottle of "spicy habanero barbeque sauce". In my area, our local grocery store produces its own line of gourmet condiments and this is from that line of products. It added the perfect amount of smokiness and spiciness. If you can find something similar I highly recommend it. I cooked the meatballs as the recipe indicates and then put everything into the crockpot on low for nearly 3 hours. Perfect amount of time and probably could have gone on longer for more flavor infusion. My husband loved them and ate the few leftover as a midnight snack, cold! Good luck!

Nummy!!!  Even with frozen meatballs, which is what I used.  I bet with the homemade meatballs they're even better...

text:
Absolutely love this recipe!! These meatballs are a huge hit every time I make them, dinner, snack, potlucks, everything! I have tried both frozen meatballs and handmade and definitely prefer handmade, it does not taste the same! We also started cooking our meatballs in the air fryer instead of the oven, they come out perfect every time. 12 minutes at 360, shake them a couple times while cooking and voila! We have also browned them in a skillet but the air fryer is the win and makes for easy cleanup. You will not go wrong with this recipe!!

text:
Great recipe!
I know some people can be disappointed that reviews are sent out changing a recipe.....but to me it's helpful to read what works for others.  So with that said...... per reading reviews this is what I did:  I DOUBLED RECIPE.  1-1/2 c bread crumbs (not Italian), 3/4 pkg Llipton onion soup mix, 1 whole can jellied cranberries, 3 T worcestershire, 3 T ketchup, add extra egg making it 3 eggs, more brown sugar to taste.
Baked meatballs, made sauce. Refrig next day, heat in crockpot.  (remember I doubled recipe) Loved the sweet/tangy flavor .  It was a hit!

text:
We made this for NYE as we had the grand kids and needed kid friendly snacks. The only alteration in the recipe was a teaspoon of salt and garlic powder added to the meatballs. The rest of the recipe as written.  Kids loved them, my husband and I thought the meatball was delish but we prefer the grape jelly/chile sauce recipe. Saw so many negative reviews crabbing the sauce was inedible because it was too spicy. I think you guys used the wrong chile sauce. Look for Heinz brand. You do not want the chinese pastes or Siracha. That would be incredibly hot. Very good recipe. Came together in no time and the children, 4,5 and 6 all ate them.

text:
Actually a 6 star recipe. It takes a bit longer than the recipe indicates. Make the sauce first, dump all the meatball ingredients in 1 bowl. Then set everything up, frying pan, butter/oil in pan, paper towels on side of stove, pan ready to put them in, utensils. Then with 2 rubber gloves on mix the meat mixture. If it seems a bit soft, add a little more bread crumbs. Make all the meatballs and put on cookies sheet, then remove only 1 glove. The gloved hand can put the meatbals in the pan to fry. I now always make at least 2 recipes worth, believe me they will be gone. As I take them out of frying pan, put on paper towels to drain, then into baking dish. I use a 9X12 ceramic pan. You can do these the day before and bake prior to needing. Can be kept warm in a crock pot too. If any are left, they make a great meat dish for dinner the next day. Have made this recipe many times, everyone loves them & asks me to bring them.

text:
As previous reviewers recommended, I used one packet of Lipton Onion soup in place of the minced onions. Otherwise, I followed the recipe exactly. I made almost 40 meatballs with one pound of meat and cooked them on a broiler pan, which worked great. The meatballs by themselves were simply amazing! I could have eaten all 40 by myself! I made four pounds of meatballs for a get-together. After the meatballs cooled, I froze them for about a week and put them in the fridge the night before our party. In the morning, I made the sauce and let it warm up in the crock pot, then added the meatballs and let them simmer all day. The amount of sauce was perfect for the number of meatballs, but I thought it was too sweet (my husband agreed). All but about 5 or 6 meatballs were eaten and people seemed to like them, but, in the future, I will make this without the brown sugar.

text:
This is a terrific recipe.  As others have said, it is a nice change from the grape jelly cocktail meatballs.  

One note, make sure you pick up the jellied cranberry sauce, instead of the ones with the cranberries in tack.  It is definitely more tangy if don't get the jellied cranberry sauce.  I didn't catch this mistake, until the second time I had made it; definitely a better balance between the sweetness and the tangyness of the sauce

text:
I really enjoyed the sauce.  I probably would have liked a little more mustard flavor (I estimated the percent of the can of cranberry and I might have put in too much which diluted the mustardy flavor of the chili sauce - I'll be more careful next time).  When tasting the meatballs, I thought they seemed a bit on the bland side but thought that was probably so the flavor of the meatball wouldn't over shadow the flavor of the sauce.  If I were to do this again, I think I will add a little brown mustard or salt to the meatballs (worcestershire seems like it might overpower the delicate flavor of the sauce) and probably skip the brown sugar and lemon juice.  Overall, a terrific holiday recipe.  I will make it again.  Thanks for sharing!

I double this and use 1 lb. ground beef and 1 lb. ground turkey (mix it thoroughly and nobody ever notices!) I've started adding a little pepper and garlic powder to the meat mixture, and using some broth instead of water.  It seems to kick it up a notch.

text:
These meatballs are fantastic! They are not spicy at all from the chili sauce. My kids were eating them and didn't find them spicy either. I made it exactly like the recipe said except I used store bought meatballs. I cook mine in a slow cooker for about 4 hours on low and then transfer to my fry daddy to keep them on warm. My slow cooker, on low, was burning the sauce. After being on warm for about 6 hours, the meatballs were so tender because the sauce cooked all the way through. I am now having to make these again for our friends open-house gathering. One of these days I would like to try this with some hot pepper sauce. Bet the sweet and spicy flavor would be awesome. Thanks for sharing such a great and easy recipe. Its a favorite around here now.

Wow, these were so good!! This recipe really deserves more than 5 stars!! My mom and I are in love with these little meatballs, and neither of us are huge meat fans either.  I think that one thing that made these meatballs so rich is that we toasted about 2 slices of white bread and tore them into small bits (as opposed to bread crumbs). The sauce is really what makes this recipe fantastic, and next time I am going to double the amount of ingredients used to make it (lemon juice, sugar, cranberry sauce, and chilli sauce), just so we will have twice as mush sauce :-)  Thanks so much for this recipe!

text:
I made this for a Christmas party, and unbeknownst to me another family member made the traditional version with grape jelly. 

Keeping in mind Ive never made them before - any version - and that Ive not tasted any version of them in probably 15 years (so I have no memory of the flavor), I can honestly say this version is more flavorful, and less sweet, and Id make them again for sure.

Notes:

- ran out of time to make my own meatballs. I couldnt find frozen meatballs at 3/4 stores I tried (is this just a Northern Virginia issue???), but Safeway came through with Rosina brand Angus Beef frozen meatballs. Theyre larger than Id have made myself, but worked fine. They are not Italian, but do have a mild seasoning of garlic, onion and bell pepper - which worked just fine as those are also in chili sauce.

- used Organics 365 cranberry jelly, which has less sugar, no HFCS,  and a really nice tart flavor

- used 2/3 Heinz chili sauce, but I made multiple batches and they only had 2 jars left, so my 3rd was a jar of a family brand that I found out later has quite a cult following, called Homade Chilli Sauce. The jar is the shape and size of a softball, and was delicious (and no corn syrup - but does have sesame seeds, which I know some people are allergic too). 

While I generally oppose making special occasion comfort food dishes like this healthy because its a treat, bot a meal staple, if its easy to do it without compromising the flavor then why not? 

In this ca

Made this for my father's 90th birthday celebration. Because the party was put together on fairly short notice, I looked for an easy, yet good appetizer to bring. Worked like a charm. text:
Fantastic! Only change I made is to use Lipton Onion Soup Mix, rather than chopped onion as suggested by other reviewers. I doubled this recipe and got 46 meatballs from two pounds of ground beef. With a pasta casserole, three adults polished off 30  meatballs for dinner! I'm definitely making this again.  It's extremely easy to make, not overly sweet, and the meatballs hold together very well. I cooked them on high in the pressure cooker (cold from fridge as I made the meatballs and sauce the night before) for about two hours. If you're going to make them for a party, I'd switch to low or keep warm after 2 to 3 hours depending on how hot your slow cooker runs.  For reference, I made these in a 7 quart slow cooker and  I think for that size slow cooker, you could easily use 5 to 6 lbs of meat.  If you plan on making these for a party, I recommend making the meatballs in advance, freeze them, and then defrost before using to save time. Great recipe for dinner, potlucks, or parties.

text:
I honestly hate meatballs. I never eat them. My friend wanted me to make these for her baby shower so if course I said yes and made them. They were honestly delicious! Here's the changes I made: I doubled the meat, eggs, and bread crumbs. Instead of minced onions, I used a packet of dry onion mix soup. I used 3/4 a can of jellied cranberries. I used chicken broth instead of water. I would have used beef broth, but I didn't have any on hand. I used Italian Seasoning, Garlic Powder, and Parsley to season the meat. I didn't measure them, just eye balled. For the sauce, I made my own mixture. I used mainly ketchup for the base and added a little  A1 sauce and Worcestershire sauce. I used lemon juice per recipe, garlic powder, and 2 bay leaves. I simmer the sauce on low on the stove top. Flipped the meatballs halfway through cooking, and put the meatballs with sauce in a crockpot to stay warm when finished

I used this sauce along with my own tried-and-true meatball recipe, and served them at a large graduation party last weekend. I made 12 lbs of meatballs ahead of time (sized about 18 meatballs per pound) and froze them until the big day. text:
Wow.  This was such a hit with kids and adults at my christmas party.  It definitely had a "meatloaf"ish taste to it, and I made the recipe exactly as stated including the meatballs from scratch.  I think this was due to the Heinz brand chili sauce that doesnt taste much different than ketchup, and the onion in the homemade meatballs.  I put the sauce ingredients in a slow cooker on high and mixed them up while the meatballs were cooking.  Then transferred the meatballs when done and turned the slow cooker to low.  The sauce was to die for.  I could have eaten it by itself with a spoon.  My sister makes a similar recipe with frozen meatballs, grape jelly and the same chili sauce, and to me it doesnt even compare.  Try this with homemade meatballs as stated instead of frozen and it's a completely different and BETTER taste.  The lemon, brown sugar, and cranberry sauce really made this unique!  Will make again VERY soon.

text:
I made these first for a small gathering...and am making changes for my larger batch- so I did make some changes according to the post suggestions...that being said...don't substitute ketchup for the water, the chili sauce is already close to ketchup. I did add the soy sauce to the sauce...liked...added the parsley to the meatballs....liked.  On the sauce though...it was still to 'ketchup-y' for me so I doubled the soy sauce I added (I never put water in it) and then put in some (2 Tbsp) hot sauce I had (specialty- I don't think I'd recommend something like Franks or Cholula). I am following suggestions again and have cooked the meatballs and made the sauce, I poured the sauce over the cooked meatballs and letting it all sit overnight to meld together....everyone loved these meatballs!

One thing- don't use too lean of a meat- I used ground beef from our cow and it was too lean, not enough fat to hold it all together. The second batch I mixed ground chuck to my lean beef 50-50.

I hope these suggestions help someone else!  And, thank you everyone for posting ideas....I rarely ever follow a recipe as written  and love reading the personalized ideas! Thank you!

text:
Well, it was okaaayy. A lot of people liked them but I was really disappointed by the taste.  The only change I made was using half ground turkey/half ground beef and then I added just a dash of worcestshire sauce like some of the reviews suggested.  I wish I had added more bc that might have given it some actual flavor.  I love sweet,  but this was sweet with no depth.  The sauce almost tasted like spaghettios to me. The meatballs before i put them in the sauce had no taste.  I noticed that there was no seasoning in the recipe,  even salt, and you can taste the lack of spice.  I think the recommendation to swap the diced onions for lipton onion soup mix is smart and would add more seasoning to it.  Also the heinz chili sauce was like glorified ketchup to me.  Next time I would try maybe a Thai sweet chili sauce for more tang,  or i would add some chili flakes (just to give it a small touch of spice, nothing too strong,  but so that it's not so 1 dimensional.) I do appreciate the simplicity of the recipe and with tweaks I do think it could be very good. I was the one who was the most critical,  everyone did seem to like it and they ate them,  so they were at least passable.

These cute little balls were a hit! I took this and the fruit salsa to a baby shower and was thoroughly enjoyed by all! I took my time and had to make a few teeny tweaks to get the sauce just right. The original recipe calls for a slightly sweet taste, and I added pinches of salt until it was perfectly balanced. text:
I don't consider myself a fabulous cook but I do like try new things and although I've tasted this sort of dish a few times in the past, I really liked mine the best. I read the reviews before making this recipe, I took some ideas while others I ignored. For example, one suggestion was doubling up on all the ingredients if using a whole can of jellied cranberry sauce. Sooo glad I did that, it was awesome. Another was to make the sauce the night before but I just didn't have enough time so I simmered it longer to really get the juices in there. Since it WAS so last minute, I had to make due with what I had on hand. One person wrote never to use frozen Italian meatballs as the sauce doesn't mix well with the spices. I took a chance - it's what I had in the freezer and again, so glad I did. I thought the mixture was terrific and they really complimented each other. Please be advised that person only cooked their meatballs in the sauce for about an hour. I left mine in the crock pot on low heat for about 4 hours, I thought they were perfect. Maybe the slow simmer really mixed it up, not sure, remember...amateur level here!

text:
Made exactly as listed except I added 1/2 tsp Italian seasoning  to the plain bread crumbs. Favors worked fine. I mixed the meat combo up the day before and made them into meatballs. I also mixed the sauce up the day before and put it in the crockpot in the refrigerator. The morning of my lunch need, I put the crockpot with sauce on low for 45 minutes and baked the meatballs for 23 minutes turning once at about 10 minutes. I put the meatballs in the crockpot sauce on low for 1.5 hrs and then warm to serve. Meatballs need to be baked to solidify and make sure they are thoroughly cooked through. They did not shred in the sauce this way.  I made 60 (2lbs of 90% ground beef) for a pass a dish. They were gone quickly as people went back for more after they tried them. No grease when they were baked. Just a nice mild appetizer.

text:
I've been making this for decades and it's always a crowd-pleaser at cocktail parties, showers, game parties and pot-lucks. When I make the meatballs from scratch I often add fresh parsley or thyme, depending on my mood.  When I'm in a rush, I forego making the meatballs and use high-quality, frozen store-bought ones -- baked in the oven according to package directions. The beauty of that is that by the time you assemble and cook the sauce, the meatballs are ready to be fired into the sauce. 
I agree with other reviewers that if a full can of cranberry sauce is used, this recipe makes more sauce than is necessary. Definitely double up the meatballs -- they won't go to waste!

text:
These are fantastic!  We hosted a large party recently and I made a double batch of these.  Oh so very good, and pretty simple as well.  I will most certainly be making these again.  The only thing I did differently was use 1/2 beef and 1/2 pork, but I'm sure they'd be good no matter what meat you use.  Oh, and I didn't turn the meatballs over in the middle of cooking, either.  With so many of them I just thought that would take forever and didn't want to take the time since we had so much other food to prepare.  They did have a slightly flattish spot that was browner than the rest of the ball, but really a non-issue.

I made the meatballs using lipton onion soup mix and i cooked them on a cooling rack so that the meatballs would not sit and cook in the grease.  They were good, but the sauce was not that great.  It was pretty thin and did not seem to stay on the meatballs very well. text:
The recipe as-is was just okay. The second time around I used panko bread crumbs, added garlic to the minced onions, and added salt, black pepper, thyme and red pepper flakes to the mixture. Then, I let it all sit overnight in the fridge. I added some cranberry pepper jelly I had on hand to the sauce mixture, a couple tbs of BBQ sauce, and sriracha. The next morning I baked the meatballs for about 10 minutes before throwing everything in the crockpot. Delicious!

text:
I've tried the grape jelly and chili sauce combo and everyone thought it just had an odd taste, but this is absolutely fantastic. The combination of the cranberry sauce and chili sauce is awesome.  I followed another reviewers advice and used a package of onion soup mix, a handful of bread crumbs, tsp. of worcheshire sauce and baked them for approx. 12 minutes at approx. 400 deg.  I let them cool, then froze them.  Just one less thing to do before my cocktail party.  On the day of - heated the chili sauce mixture (this I followed exactly including the lemon juice and brown sugar) in a saucepan, put my frozen meat balls also in the sauce pan, gave it a quick stir to get them evenly coated and poured into my slow cooker to finish heating and glazing.  Thank you very much Lara for sharing this recipe.  No more grape junk ever again!!!!

I've made these twice now for large parties and followed the recipe exactly each time (for both the meatballs and the sauce).  I thought the texture of the meatballs was very good -- not too hard or rubbery.  I totally disagree with reviewers who claim the sauce was spicy.  I didn't thing this was the case at all; in fact they were sweet and tangy.  While I thought the overall dish was decent, I've never received a compliment or request for the recipe.  At the end of the party there were more left in the pot than gone.  Perhaps I just had too much other food.  As a result, I think I'll keep looking for the perfect cocktail meatball recipe.
